### Humans

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/20211109_Frequency_of_extreme_weather_for_different_degrees_of_global_warming_-_bar_chart_IPCC_AR6_WG1_SPM.svg/500px-20211109_Frequency_of_extreme_weather_for_different_degrees_of_global_warming_-_bar_chart_IPCC_AR6_WG1_SPM.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:20211109_Frequency_of_extreme_weather_for_different_degrees_of_global_warming_-_bar_chart_IPCC_AR6_WG1_SPM.svg)

Extreme weather will be progressively more common as the Earth warms.[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC6AR_ExtremeEvents-239)

The effects of climate change are impacting humans everywhere in the world.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-240) Impacts can be observed on all continents and ocean regions,[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-241) with low-latitude, [less developed areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_country "Developing country") facing the greatest risk.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-242) Continued warming has potentially "severe, pervasive and irreversible impacts" for people and ecosystems.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-243) The risks are unevenly distributed, but are generally greater for disadvantaged people in developing and developed countries.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-244)

#### Health and food

The [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") calls climate change one of the biggest threats to global health in the 21st century.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-WHO_Nov_2023-14) Scientists have warned about the irreversible harms it poses.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Romanello_et_al_2023-245)[Extreme weather](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_weather "Extreme weather") events affect public health, and [food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_security "Food security") and [water security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_security "Water security").[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-nca2018_ch14-246)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Romanello_et_al_2022-247)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC_AR6_WG2_p9-248)[Temperature extremes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change#Heat_waves_and_temperature_extremes "Effects of climate change") lead to increased illness and death.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-nca2018_ch14-246)[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Romanello_et_al_2022-247) Climate change increases the intensity and frequency of extreme weather events.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Romanello_et_al_2022-247)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC_AR6_WG2_p9-248) It can affect transmission of [infectious diseases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infectious_diseases "Infectious diseases"), such as [dengue fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dengue_fever "Dengue fever") and [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria").[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Romanello_et_al_2023-245)[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-nca2018_ch14-246) According to the [World Economic Forum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Economic_Forum "World Economic Forum"), 14.5 million more deaths are expected due to climate change by 2050.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-249) 30% of the global population currently live in areas where extreme heat and humidity are already associated with excess deaths.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Carbon_Brief_2017-250)[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-251) By 2100, 50% to 75% of the global population would live in such areas.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Carbon_Brief_2017-250)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-252)

While total [crop yields](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crop_yield "Crop yield") have been increasing in the past 50 years due to agricultural improvements, [climate change has already decreased the rate of yield growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_agriculture "Effects of climate change on agriculture").[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC_AR6_WG2_p9-248)[Fisheries have been negatively affected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_and_fisheries "Climate change and fisheries") in multiple regions.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC_AR6_WG2_p9-248) While [agricultural productivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricultural_productivity "Agricultural productivity") has been positively affected in some high [latitude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latitude "Latitude") areas, mid- and low-latitude areas have been negatively affected.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC_AR6_WG2_p9-248) According to the World Economic Forum, an increase in drought in certain regions could cause 3.2 million deaths from [malnutrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malnutrition "Malnutrition") by 2050 and [stunting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stunted_growth "Stunted growth") in children.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-253) With 2°C warming, global livestock headcounts could decline by 7–10% by 2050, as less animal feed will be available.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-254) If the emissions continue to increase for the rest of century, then over 9 million climate-related deaths would occur annually by 2100.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-255)

#### Livelihoods and inequality

Economic damages due to climate change may be severe and there is a chance of disastrous consequences.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-256) Severe impacts are expected in South-East Asia and [sub-Saharan Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Africa "Climate change in Africa"), where most of the local inhabitants are dependent upon natural and agricultural resources.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FAO-2021-257)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-258)[Heat stress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_stress "Heat stress") can prevent outdoor labourers from working. If warming reaches 4°C then labour capacity in those regions could be reduced by 30 to 50%.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-259) The [World Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank") estimates that between 2016 and 2030, climate change could drive over 120 million people into extreme poverty without adaptation.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHallegatteBangaloreBonzanigoFay201612-260)

Inequalities based on wealth and social status have worsened due to climate change.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-261) Major difficulties in mitigating, adapting to, and recovering from climate shocks are faced by marginalized people who have less control over resources.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Grabe-2014-262)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FAO-2021-257)[Indigenous people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indigenous_people "Indigenous people"), who are subsistent on their land and ecosystems, will face endangerment to their wellness and lifestyles due to climate change.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-263) An expert elicitation concluded that the role of climate change in [armed conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_conflict "Armed conflict") has been small compared to factors such as socio-economic inequality and state capabilities.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMachKraanAdgerBuhaug2019-264)

While women are not inherently more at risk from climate change and shocks, limits on women's resources and discriminatory gender norms constrain their adaptive capacity and resilience.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FAO-2023-265) For example, women's work burdens, including hours worked in agriculture, tend to decline less than men's during climate shocks such as heat stress.[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FAO-2023-265)

#### Climate migration

Low-lying islands and coastal communities are threatened by sea level rise, which makes [urban flooding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_flooding "Urban flooding") more common. Sometimes, land is permanently lost to the sea.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_SROCC_Ch42019328-266) This could lead to [statelessness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statelessness "Statelessness") for people in island nations, such as the [Maldives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maldives "Maldives") and [Tuvalu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuvalu "Tuvalu").[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-267) In some regions, the rise in temperature and humidity may be too severe for humans to adapt to.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthews2018399-268) With worst-case climate change, models project that areas almost one-third of humanity live in might become Sahara-like uninhabitable and extremely hot climates.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-269)

These factors can drive [climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_migrant "Climate migrant") or [environmental migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_migrant "Environmental migrant"), within and between countries.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Cattaneo-2019-270) More people are expected to be displaced because of sea level rise, extreme weather and conflict from increased competition over natural resources. Climate change may also increase vulnerability, leading to "trapped populations" who are not able to move due to a lack of resources.[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-271)

Reducing and recapturing emissions
----------------------------------

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Greenhouse_gas_emission_scenarios_01.svg/500px-Greenhouse_gas_emission_scenarios_01.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Greenhouse_gas_emission_scenarios_01.svg)

Global greenhouse gas emission scenarios, based on policies and pledges as of November 2021

Climate change can be mitigated by reducing the rate at which greenhouse gases are emitted into the atmosphere, and by increasing the rate at which carbon dioxide is removed from the atmosphere.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-277) To limit global warming to less than 1.5°C global greenhouse gas emissions needs to be [net-zero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_neutrality "Carbon neutrality") by 2050, or by 2070 with a 2°C target.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC-2018_p12-278) This requires far-reaching, systemic changes on an unprecedented scale in energy, land, cities, transport, buildings, and industry.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-279)

The [United Nations Environment Programme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme "United Nations Environment Programme") estimates that countries need to triple their [pledges under the Paris Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationally_determined_contribution "Nationally determined contribution") within the next decade to limit global warming to 2°C. An even greater level of reduction is required to meet the 1.5°C goal.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-280) With pledges made under the Paris Agreement as of 2024, there would be a 66% chance that global warming is kept under 2.8°C by the end of the century (range: 1.9–3.7°C, depending on exact implementation and technological progress). When only considering current policies, this raises to 3.1°C.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_Nations_Environment_Programme202433,_34-281) Globally, limiting warming to 2°C may result in higher economic benefits than economic costs.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-282)

Although there is no single pathway to limit global warming to 1.5 or 2°C,[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-283) most scenarios and strategies see a major increase in the use of renewable energy in combination with increased energy efficiency measures to generate the needed greenhouse gas reductions.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Teske,_ed._2019_xxiii-284) To reduce pressures on ecosystems and enhance their carbon sequestration capabilities, changes would also be necessary in agriculture and forestry,[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-285) such as preventing [deforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation "Deforestation") and restoring natural ecosystems by [reforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reforestation "Reforestation").[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-286)

Other approaches to mitigating climate change have a higher level of risk. Scenarios that limit global warming to 1.5°C typically project the large-scale use of [carbon dioxide removal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_removal "Carbon dioxide removal") methods over the 21st century.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-287) There are concerns, though, about over-reliance on these technologies, and environmental impacts.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-288)

[Solar radiation modification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_radiation_modification "Solar radiation modification") (SRM) is a proposal for reducing global warming by reflecting some sunlight away from Earth and back into space. Because it does not reduce greenhouse gas concentrations, it would not address ocean acidification[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-289) and is not considered mitigation.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-290) SRM should be considered only as a supplement to mitigation, not a replacement for it,[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-291) due to risks such as rapid warming if it were abruptly stopped and not restarted.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-292) The most-studied approach is [stratospheric aerosol injection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stratospheric_aerosol_injection "Stratospheric aerosol injection").[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-auto-293) SRM could reduce global warming and some of its impacts, though imperfectly.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-294) It poses environmental risks, such as changes to rainfall patterns,[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-295) as well as political challenges, such as who would decide whether to use it.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-auto-293)

### Clean energy

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Global_Energy_Consumption.svg/500px-Global_Energy_Consumption.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Global_Energy_Consumption.svg)

Coal, oil, and natural gas remain the primary [global energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_energy_consumption "World energy consumption") sources even as [renewables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy "Renewable energy") have begun rapidly increasing.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-296)

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Lisberg_Burg_Windr%C3%A4der_Solar_power_PC313027.jpg/500px-Lisberg_Burg_Windr%C3%A4der_Solar_power_PC313027.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lisberg_Burg_Windr%C3%A4der_Solar_power_PC313027.jpg)

Wind and solar power, Germany

Renewable energy is key to limiting climate change.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-United_Nations_Environment_Programme_2019_46-297) For decades, fossil fuels have accounted for roughly 80% of the world's energy use.[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-298) The remaining share has been split between nuclear power and renewables (including [hydropower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydropower "Hydropower"), [bioenergy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioenergy "Bioenergy"), wind and solar power and [geothermal energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geothermal_energy "Geothermal energy")).[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-299) Fossil fuel use is expected to peak in absolute terms prior to 2030 and then to decline, with coal use experiencing the sharpest reductions.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-300) Renewables represented 86% of all new electricity generation installed in 2023.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IRENA-301) Other forms of clean energy, such as nuclear and hydropower, currently have a larger share of the energy supply. However, their future growth forecasts appear limited in comparison.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-302)

While [solar panels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photovoltaic_system "Photovoltaic system") and onshore wind are now among the cheapest forms of adding new power generation capacity in many locations,[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-303) green energy policies are needed to achieve a rapid transition from fossil fuels to renewables.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-304) To achieve carbon neutrality by 2050, renewable energy would become the dominant form of electricity generation, rising to 85% or more by 2050 in some scenarios. Investment in coal would be eliminated and coal use nearly phased out by 2050.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-305)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-306)

Electricity generated from renewable sources would also need to become the main energy source for heating and transport.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-307) Transport can switch away from [internal combustion engine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine "Internal combustion engine") vehicles and towards [electric vehicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_vehicle "Electric vehicle"), public transit, and [active transport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active_mobility "Active mobility") (cycling and walking).[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC-2018_p142-308)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-309) For shipping and flying, low-carbon fuels would reduce emissions.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC-2018_p142-308) Heating could be increasingly decarbonized with technologies like [heat pumps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_pump "Heat pump").[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-310)

There are obstacles to the continued rapid growth of clean energy, including renewables.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-311) Wind and solar produce energy [intermittently and with seasonal variability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable_renewable_energy "Variable renewable energy"). Traditionally, [hydro dams with reservoirs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pumped-storage_hydroelectricity "Pumped-storage hydroelectricity") and fossil fuel power plants have been used when variable energy production is low. Going forward, [battery storage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battery_storage_power_station "Battery storage power station") can be expanded, [energy demand and supply](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demand_response "Demand response") can be matched, and long-distance [transmission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_power_transmission "Electric power transmission") can smooth variability of renewable outputs.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-United_Nations_Environment_Programme_2019_46-297) Bioenergy is often not carbon-neutral and may have negative consequences for food security.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-312) The growth of nuclear power is constrained by controversy around [radioactive waste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radioactive_waste "Radioactive waste"), [nuclear weapon proliferation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation "Nuclear proliferation"), and [accidents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_accident "Nuclear accident").[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-313)[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-314) Hydropower growth is limited by the fact that the best sites have been developed, and new projects are confronting increased social and environmental concerns.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-315)

[Low-carbon energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life-cycle_greenhouse_gas_emissions_of_energy_sources "Life-cycle greenhouse gas emissions of energy sources") improves human health by minimizing climate change as well as reducing air pollution deaths,[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-316) which were estimated at 7 million annually in 2016.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-317) Meeting the Paris Agreement goals that limit warming to a 2°C increase could save about a million of those lives per year by 2050, whereas limiting global warming to 1.5°C could save millions and simultaneously increase [energy security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_security "Energy security") and reduce poverty.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-318) Improving air quality also has economic benefits which may be larger than mitigation costs.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-319)

### Energy conservation

Reducing energy demand is another major aspect of reducing emissions.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-320) If less energy is needed, there is more flexibility for clean energy development. It also makes it easier to manage the electricity grid, and minimizes [carbon-intensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emission_intensity "Emission intensity") infrastructure development.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-321) Major increases in energy efficiency investment will be required to achieve climate goals, comparable to the level of investment in renewable energy.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-322) Several [COVID-19](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic") related changes in energy use patterns, energy efficiency investments, and funding have made forecasts for this decade more difficult and uncertain.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-323)

Strategies to reduce energy demand vary by sector. In the transport sector, passengers and freight can switch to more efficient travel modes, such as buses and trains, or use electric vehicles.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-324) Industrial strategies to reduce energy demand include improving heating systems and motors, designing less energy-intensive products, and increasing product lifetimes.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-325) In the building sector the focus is on better design of new buildings, and higher levels of energy efficiency in retrofitting.[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-326) The use of technologies like heat pumps can also increase building energy efficiency.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-327)

### Agriculture and industry

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_by_Economic_Sector.svg/500px-Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_by_Economic_Sector.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Greenhouse_Gas_Emissions_by_Economic_Sector.svg)

Taking into account direct and indirect emissions, industry is the sector with the highest share of global emissions. Data as of 2019 from the IPCC.

Agriculture and forestry face a triple challenge of limiting greenhouse gas emissions, preventing the further conversion of forests to agricultural land, and meeting increases in world food demand.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-328) A set of actions could reduce agriculture and forestry-based emissions by two-thirds from 2010 levels. These include reducing growth in demand for food and other agricultural products, increasing land productivity, protecting and restoring forests, and reducing greenhouse gas emissions from agricultural production.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-329)

On the demand side, a key component of reducing emissions is shifting people towards [plant-based diets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant-based_diets "Plant-based diets").[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-330) Eliminating the production of livestock for [meat and dairy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_meat_production "Environmental impact of meat production") would eliminate about 3/4ths of all emissions from agriculture and other land use.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-331) Livestock also occupy 37% of ice-free land area on Earth and consume feed from the 12% of land area used for crops, driving deforestation and land degradation.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-332)

Steel and cement production are responsible for about 13% of industrial CO 2 emissions. In these industries, carbon-intensive materials such as coke and lime play an integral role in the production, so that reducing CO 2 emissions requires research into alternative chemistries.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-333) Where energy production or CO 2-intensive [heavy industries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavy_industry "Heavy industry") continue to produce waste CO 2, technology can sometimes be used to capture and store most of the gas instead of releasing it to the atmosphere.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-:22-334) This technology, [carbon capture and storage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage "Carbon capture and storage") (CCS), could have a critical but limited role in reducing emissions.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-:22-334) It is relatively expensive[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-335) and has been deployed only to an extent that removes around 0.1% of annual greenhouse gas emissions.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-:22-334)

### Carbon dioxide removal

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Carbon_Dioxide_Partitioning.svg/500px-Carbon_Dioxide_Partitioning.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Carbon_Dioxide_Partitioning.svg)

Most CO 2 emissions have been absorbed by [carbon sinks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_sink "Carbon sink"), including plant growth, soil uptake, and ocean uptake ([2020 Global Carbon Budget](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Carbon_Project#Global_Carbon_Budget "Global Carbon Project")).

Natural carbon sinks can be enhanced to sequester significantly larger amounts of CO 2 beyond naturally occurring levels.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-336) Reforestation and [afforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afforestation "Afforestation") (planting forests where there were none before) are among the most mature sequestration techniques, although the latter raises food security concerns.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-337) Farmers can promote sequestration of [carbon in soils](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_farming "Carbon farming") through practices such as use of winter [cover crops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cover_crops "Cover crops"), reducing the intensity and frequency of [tillage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tillage "Tillage"), and using compost and manure as soil amendments.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-338) Forest and landscape restoration yields many benefits for the climate, including greenhouse gas emissions sequestration and reduction.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Duchelle-2022-134) Restoration/recreation of coastal wetlands, [prairie plots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prairie_restoration "Prairie restoration") and [seagrass meadows](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seagrass_meadow "Seagrass meadow") increases the uptake of carbon into organic matter.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-339)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-340) When carbon is sequestered in soils and in organic matter such as trees, there is a risk of the carbon being re-released into the atmosphere later through changes in land use, fire, or other changes in ecosystems.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-341)

The use of bioenergy in conjunction with carbon capture and storage ([BECCS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bioenergy_with_carbon_capture_and_storage "Bioenergy with carbon capture and storage")) can result in net negative emissions as CO 2 is drawn from the atmosphere.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-342) It remains highly uncertain whether carbon dioxide removal techniques will be able to play a large role in limiting warming to 1.5°C. Policy decisions that rely on carbon dioxide removal increase the risk of global warming rising beyond international goals.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-343)

Adaptation
----------

Adaptation is "the process of adjustment to current or expected changes in climate and its effects".[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-IPCC-2022-344): 5  Without additional mitigation, adaptation cannot avert the risk of "severe, widespread and irreversible" impacts.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_AR5_SYR201417-345) More severe climate change requires more transformative adaptation, which can be prohibitively expensive.[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_SR15_Ch42018396%E2%80%93397-346) The [capacity and potential for humans to adapt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptive_capacity "Adaptive capacity") is unevenly distributed across different regions and populations, and developing countries generally have less.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-347) The first two decades of the 21st century saw an increase in adaptive capacity in most low- and middle-income countries with improved access to basic [sanitation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanitation "Sanitation") and electricity, but progress is slow. Many countries have implemented adaptation policies. However, there is a considerable gap between necessary and available finance.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNEP2018xii%E2%80%93xiii-348)

Adaptation to sea level rise consists of avoiding at-risk areas, learning to live with increased flooding, and building [flood controls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flood_control "Flood control"). If that fails, [managed retreat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Managed_retreat "Managed retreat") may be needed.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-349) There are economic barriers for tackling dangerous heat impact. Avoiding strenuous work or having [air conditioning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_conditioning "Air conditioning") is not possible for everybody.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthews2018402-350) In agriculture, adaptation options include a switch to more sustainable diets, diversification, erosion control, and genetic improvements for increased tolerance to a changing climate.[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_SRCCL_Ch52019439-351) Insurance allows for risk-sharing, but is often difficult to get for people on lower incomes.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-352) Education, migration and [early warning systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_warning_system "Early warning system") can reduce climate vulnerability.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_SR15_Ch42018336%E2%80%93337-353) Planting mangroves or encouraging other coastal vegetation can buffer storms.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-354)[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-355)

Ecosystems adapt to climate change, a process that can be supported by human intervention. By increasing connectivity between ecosystems, species can migrate to more favourable climate conditions. Species can also be [introduced to areas acquiring a favourable climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assisted_migration "Assisted migration"). Protection and restoration of natural and semi-natural areas helps build resilience, making it easier for ecosystems to adapt. Many of the actions that promote adaptation in ecosystems, also help humans adapt via [ecosystem-based adaptation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecosystem-based_adaptation "Ecosystem-based adaptation"). For instance, restoration of [natural fire regimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fire_regime "Fire regime") makes catastrophic fires less likely, and reduces human exposure. Giving rivers more space allows for more water storage in the natural system, reducing flood risk. Restored forest acts as a carbon sink, but planting trees in unsuitable regions can exacerbate climate impacts.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-356)

There are [synergies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Synergy "Synergy") but also trade-offs between adaptation and mitigation.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-357) An example for synergy is increased food productivity, which has large benefits for both adaptation and mitigation.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-358) An example of a trade-off is that increased use of air conditioning [allows people to better cope with heat, but increases energy demand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_conditioning_paradox "Air conditioning paradox"). Another trade-off example is that more compact [urban development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_planning "Urban planning") may reduce emissions from transport and construction, but may also increase the [urban heat island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_heat_island "Urban heat island") effect, exposing people to heat-related health risks.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-359)

**Examples of adaptation methods***   [![Image 36: Mangrove planting and other habitat conservation can reduce coastal flooding.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/FrontLines-EGAT_2011_Environment_Photo_Contest_Top_Entry_%285842818280%29.jpg/330px-FrontLines-EGAT_2011_Environment_Photo_Contest_Top_Entry_%285842818280%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:FrontLines-EGAT_2011_Environment_Photo_Contest_Top_Entry_(5842818280).jpg "Mangrove planting and other habitat conservation can reduce coastal flooding.")

[Mangrove](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mangrove "Mangrove") planting and other [habitat conservation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat_conservation "Habitat conservation") can reduce [coastal flooding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_flooding "Coastal flooding"). 
*   [![Image 37: Seawalls to protect against storm surge worsened by sea level rise](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Seawallventnor.jpg/250px-Seawallventnor.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seawallventnor.jpg "Seawalls to protect against storm surge worsened by sea level rise")

[Seawalls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seawall "Seawall") to protect against [storm surge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Storm_surge "Storm surge") worsened by [sea level rise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_level_rise "Sea level rise") 
*   [![Image 38: Green roofs to provide cooling in cities](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/20080708_Chicago_City_Hall_Green_Roof_Edit1.jpg/330px-20080708_Chicago_City_Hall_Green_Roof_Edit1.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:20080708_Chicago_City_Hall_Green_Roof_Edit1.jpg "Green roofs to provide cooling in cities")

*   [![Image 39: Selective breeding for drought-resistant crops](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/2013.02-402-294a_Pearl_millet%2Cbreeding%2Cselfing_ICRISAT%2CPatancheru%28Hyderabad%2CAndhra_Pradesh%29%2CIN_wed20feb2013.jpg/330px-2013.02-402-294a_Pearl_millet%2Cbreeding%2Cselfing_ICRISAT%2CPatancheru%28Hyderabad%2CAndhra_Pradesh%29%2CIN_wed20feb2013.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2013.02-402-294a_Pearl_millet,breeding,selfing_ICRISAT,Patancheru(Hyderabad,Andhra_Pradesh),IN_wed20feb2013.jpg "Selective breeding for drought-resistant crops")

Policies and politics
---------------------

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Climate_Change_Performance_Index_%282023%29.svg/500px-Climate_Change_Performance_Index_%282023%29.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Climate_Change_Performance_Index_(2023).svg)

The [Climate Change Performance Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_Change_Performance_Index "Climate Change Performance Index") ranks countries by greenhouse gas emissions (40% of score), renewable energy (20%), energy use (20%), and climate policy (20%). 
High Medium Low Very low No data

Countries that are most [vulnerable to climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_vulnerability "Climate change vulnerability") have typically been responsible for a small share of global emissions. This raises questions about justice and fairness.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-360) Limiting global warming makes it much easier to achieve the UN's [Sustainable Development Goals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals "Sustainable Development Goals"), such as eradicating poverty and reducing inequalities. The connection is recognized in [Sustainable Development Goal 13](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goal_13 "Sustainable Development Goal 13") which is to "take urgent action to combat climate change and its impacts".[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-361) The goals on food, clean water and ecosystem protection have synergies with climate mitigation.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIPCC_SR15_Ch52018477-362)

The [geopolitics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geopolitics "Geopolitics") of climate change is complex. It has often been framed as a [free-rider problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free-rider_problem "Free-rider problem"), in which all countries benefit from mitigation done by other countries, but individual countries would lose from switching to a [low-carbon economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low-carbon_economy "Low-carbon economy") themselves. Sometimes mitigation also has localized benefits though. For instance, the benefits of a [coal phase-out](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal_phase_out "Coal phase out") to public health and local environments exceed the costs in almost all regions.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Rauner_2020-363) Furthermore, net importers of fossil fuels win economically from switching to clean energy, causing net exporters to face [stranded assets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stranded_assets "Stranded assets"): fossil fuels they cannot sell.[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-364)

### Policy options

A wide range of [policies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Policy "Policy"), regulations, and laws are being used to reduce emissions. As of 2019, [carbon pricing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_pricing "Carbon pricing") covers about 20% of global greenhouse gas emissions.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-365) Carbon can be priced with [carbon taxes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_tax "Carbon tax") and [emissions trading systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_emission_trading "Carbon emission trading").[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-366) Direct global [fossil fuel subsidies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuel_subsidies "Fossil fuel subsidies") reached $319 billion in 2017, and $5.2 trillion when indirect costs such as air pollution are priced in.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-367) Ending these can cause a 28% reduction in global carbon emissions and a 46% reduction in air pollution deaths.[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-368) Money saved on fossil subsidies could be used to support the [transition to clean energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_transition "Renewable energy transition") instead.[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-369) More direct methods to reduce greenhouse gases include vehicle efficiency standards, renewable fuel standards, and air pollution regulations on heavy industry.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-370) Several countries [require utilities to increase the share of renewables in power production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_portfolio_standard "Renewable portfolio standard").[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-371)

#### Climate justice

Policy designed through the lens of [climate justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_justice "Climate justice") tries to address human rights issues and social inequality. According to proponents of climate justice, the costs of climate adaptation should be paid by those most responsible for climate change, while the beneficiaries of payments should be those suffering impacts. One way this can be addressed in practice is to have wealthy nations pay poorer countries to adapt.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-372)

Oxfam found that in 2023 the wealthiest 10% of people were responsible for 50% of global emissions, while the bottom 50% were responsible for just 8%.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-373) Production of emissions is another way to look at responsibility: under that approach, the top 21 fossil fuel companies would owe cumulative [climate reparations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_reparations "Climate reparations") of $5.4 trillion over the period 2025–2050.[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-OneEarth_20230519-374) To achieve a [just transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Just_transition "Just transition"), people working in the fossil fuel sector would also need other jobs, and their communities would need investments.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-375)

### International climate agreements

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Total_CO2_by_Region.svg/500px-Total_CO2_by_Region.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Total_CO2_by_Region.svg)

Since 2000, rising CO 2 emissions in China and the rest of world have surpassed the output of the United States and Europe.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Friedlingstein_2019-376)

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Per_Capita_CO2_by_Region.svg/500px-Per_Capita_CO2_by_Region.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Per_Capita_CO2_by_Region.svg)

Per person, the United States generates CO 2 at a far faster rate than other primary regions.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Friedlingstein_2019-376)

Nearly all countries in the world are parties to the 1994 [United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change "United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change") (UNFCCC).[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-377) The goal of the UNFCCC is to prevent dangerous human interference with the climate system.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-378) As stated in the convention, this requires that greenhouse gas concentrations are stabilized in the atmosphere at a level where ecosystems can adapt naturally to climate change, food production is not threatened, and [economic development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_analysis_of_climate_change "Economic analysis of climate change") can be sustained.[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-379) The UNFCCC does not itself restrict emissions but rather provides a framework for protocols that do. Global emissions have risen since the UNFCCC was signed.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-EPA-2019-380)[Its yearly conferences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Climate_Change_conference "United Nations Climate Change conference") are the stage of global negotiations.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-381)

The 1997 [Kyoto Protocol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol "Kyoto Protocol") extended the UNFCCC and included legally binding commitments for most developed countries to limit their emissions.[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-382) During the negotiations, the [G77](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_of_77 "Group of 77") (representing [developing countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_country "Developing country")) pushed for a mandate requiring [developed countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country "Developed country") to "[take] the lead" in reducing their emissions,[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-383) since developed countries contributed most to the [accumulation of greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions#Cumulative_and_historical_emissions "Greenhouse gas emissions") in the atmosphere. Per-capita emissions were also still relatively low in developing countries and developing countries would need to emit more to meet their development needs.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-384)

The 2009 [Copenhagen Accord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Copenhagen_Accord "Copenhagen Accord") has been widely portrayed as disappointing because of its low goals, and was rejected by poorer nations including the G77.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-385) Associated parties aimed to limit the global temperature rise to below 2°C.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-386) The accord set the goal of sending $100 billion per year to developing countries for mitigation and adaptation by 2020, and proposed the founding of the [Green Climate Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Climate_Fund "Green Climate Fund").[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-387) As of 2020, only 83.3 billion were delivered. Only in 2023 the target is expected to be achieved.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-388)

In 2015 all UN countries negotiated the [Paris Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Agreement "Paris Agreement"), which aims to keep global warming well below 2.0°C and contains an aspirational goal of keeping warming under 1.5°C.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParis_Agreement2015-389) The agreement replaced the Kyoto Protocol. Unlike Kyoto, no binding emission targets were set in the Paris Agreement. Instead, a set of procedures was made binding. Countries have to regularly set ever more ambitious goals and reevaluate these goals every five years.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-390) The Paris Agreement restated that developing countries must be financially supported.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-391) As of March 2025, 194 states and the European Union have acceded to or [ratified](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ratification "Ratification") the agreement.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-392)

The 1987 [Montreal Protocol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montreal_Protocol "Montreal Protocol"), an international agreement to phase out production of ozone-depleting gases, has had benefits for climate change mitigation.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-393) Several ozone-depleting gases like [chlorofluorocarbons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chlorofluorocarbons "Chlorofluorocarbons") are powerful greenhouse gases, so banning their production and usage may have avoided a temperature rise of 0.5°C–1.0°C,[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-394) as well as additional warming by preventing damage to vegetation from [ultraviolet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet") radiation.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-395) It is estimated that the agreement has been more effective at curbing greenhouse gas emissions than the Kyoto Protocol specifically designed to do so.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-396) The most recent amendment to the Montreal Protocol, the 2016 [Kigali Amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kigali_Amendment "Kigali Amendment"), committed to reducing the emissions of [hydrofluorocarbons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrofluorocarbon "Hydrofluorocarbon"), which served as a replacement for banned ozone-depleting gases and are also potent greenhouse gases.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-397) Should countries comply with the amendment, a warming of 0.3°C–0.5°C is estimated to be avoided.[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-398)

### National responses

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Annual_CO2_emissions_by_region%2C_2022.png/330px-Annual_CO2_emissions_by_region%2C_2022.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Annual_CO2_emissions_by_region,_2022.png)

Annual [CO 2 emissions by region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions "List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions"). This measures fossil fuel and industry emissions. [Land use change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_use_change "Land use change") is not included.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-399)

In 2019, the [United Kingdom parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom "Parliament of the United Kingdom") became the first national government to declare a climate emergency.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-400) Other countries and [jurisdictions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jurisdiction "Jurisdiction") followed suit.[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-401) That same year, the [European Parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament") declared a "climate and environmental emergency".[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-402) The [European Commission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission") presented its [European Green Deal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Green_Deal "European Green Deal") with the goal of making the EU carbon-neutral by 2050.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-403) In 2021, the European Commission released its "[Fit for 55](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fit_for_55 "Fit for 55")" legislation package, which contains guidelines for the [car industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry "Automotive industry"); all new cars on the European market must be [zero-emission vehicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle "Zero-emissions vehicle") from 2035.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-404)

Major countries in Asia have made similar pledges: South Korea and Japan have committed to become carbon-neutral by 2050, and China by 2060.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-405) While India has strong incentives for renewables, it also plans a significant expansion of coal in the country.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-406) Vietnam is among very few coal-dependent, fast-developing countries that pledged to phase out unabated coal power by the 2040s or as soon as possible thereafter.[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-407)

As of 2021, based on information from 48 [national climate plans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationally_Determined_Contributions "Nationally Determined Contributions"), which represent 40% of the parties to the Paris Agreement, estimated total greenhouse gas emissions will be 0.5% lower compared to 2010 levels, below the 45% or 25% reduction goals to limit global warming to 1.5°C or 2°C, respectively.[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-408)

Society and culture
-------------------

### Denial and misinformation

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/20200327_Climate_change_deniers_cherry_picking_time_periods.gif/500px-20200327_Climate_change_deniers_cherry_picking_time_periods.gif)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:20200327_Climate_change_deniers_cherry_picking_time_periods.gif)

Data has been [cherry picked](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cherry_picking "Cherry picking") from short periods to falsely assert that global temperatures are not rising. Blue trendlines show short periods that mask longer-term warming trends (red trendlines). Blue rectangle with blue dots shows the so-called [global warming hiatus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_warming_hiatus "Global warming hiatus").[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStover2014-409)

Public debate about climate change has been strongly affected by climate change denial and [misinformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misinformation "Misinformation"), which originated in the United States and has since spread to other countries, particularly Canada and Australia. Climate change denial has originated from fossil fuel companies, industry groups, conservative think tanks, and [contrarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contrarian "Contrarian") scientists.[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-410)[Like the tobacco industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tobacco_industry_playbook "Tobacco industry playbook"), the main strategy of these groups has been to manufacture doubt about climate-change related scientific data and results.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-411) People who hold unwarranted doubt about climate change are called climate change "skeptics", although "contrarians" or "deniers" are more appropriate terms.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-412)

There are different variants of climate denial: some deny that warming takes place at all, some acknowledge warming but attribute it to natural influences, and some minimize the negative impacts of climate change.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Bj%C3%B6rnberg_2017-413) Manufacturing uncertainty about the science later developed into a [manufactured controversy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manufactured_controversy "Manufactured controversy"): creating the belief that there is significant uncertainty about climate change within the scientific community to delay policy changes.[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-414) Strategies to promote these ideas include criticism of scientific institutions,[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-415) and questioning the motives of individual scientists.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Bj%C3%B6rnberg_2017-413) An [echo chamber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Echo_chamber_(media) "Echo chamber (media)") of climate-denying [blogs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blogs "Blogs") and media has further fomented misunderstanding of climate change.[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-416)

### Public awareness and opinion

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/20220629_Public_estimates_of_scientific_consensus_on_climate_change_-_horizontal_bar_chart.svg/500px-20220629_Public_estimates_of_scientific_consensus_on_climate_change_-_horizontal_bar_chart.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:20220629_Public_estimates_of_scientific_consensus_on_climate_change_-_horizontal_bar_chart.svg)

 The public substantially underestimates the degree of scientific consensus that humans are causing climate change (2022 data).[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-KingsCollegeReport_20220629-417) Studies from 2019 to 2021[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Powell_2019-418)[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Lynas_2021-4)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-419) found scientific consensus to range from 98.7 to 100%.

Climate change came to international public attention in the late 1980s.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Weart-420) Due to media coverage in the early 1990s, people often confused climate change with other environmental issues like ozone depletion.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Newell2006-421)[In popular culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_popular_culture "Climate change in popular culture"), the [climate fiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_fiction "Climate fiction") movie _[The Day After Tomorrow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Day\_After\_Tomorrow "The Day After Tomorrow")_ (2004) and the [Al Gore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Gore "Al Gore") documentary _[An Inconvenient Truth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/An\_Inconvenient\_Truth "An Inconvenient Truth")_ (2006) focused on climate change.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Weart-420)

Significant regional, gender, age and political differences exist in both public concern for, and understanding of, climate change. More highly educated people, and in some countries, women and younger people, were more likely to see climate change as a serious threat.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-422) College biology textbooks from the 2010s featured less content on climate change compared to those from the preceding decade, with decreasing emphasis on solutions.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-:0-423) Partisan gaps also exist in many countries,[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-424) and countries with high [CO 2 emissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CO2_emissions "CO2 emissions") tend to be less concerned.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-425) Views on causes of climate change vary widely between countries.[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-426) Media coverage linked to protests has had impacts on public sentiment as well as on which aspects of climate change are focused upon.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-427) Higher levels of worry are associated with stronger public support for policies that address climate change.[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-428) Concern has increased over time,[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-429) and in 2021 a majority of citizens in 30 countries expressed a high level of worry about climate change, or view it as a global emergency.[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-430) A 2024 survey across 125 countries found that 89% of the global population demanded intensified political action, but systematically [underestimated other peoples'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluralistic_ignorance "Pluralistic ignorance") willingness to act.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Damian-26)[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Peter-27)

#### Climate movement

Climate protests demand that political leaders take action to prevent climate change. They can take the form of public demonstrations, [fossil fuel divestment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuel_divestment "Fossil fuel divestment"), lawsuits and other activities.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-431)[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-432) Prominent demonstrations include the [School Strike for Climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_Strike_for_Climate "School Strike for Climate"). In this initiative, young people across the globe have been protesting since 2018 by skipping school on Fridays, inspired by Swedish activist and then-teenager [Greta Thunberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greta_Thunberg "Greta Thunberg").[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-433) Mass [civil disobedience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_disobedience "Civil disobedience") actions by groups like [Extinction Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinction_Rebellion "Extinction Rebellion") have protested by disrupting roads and public transport.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-434)

[Litigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_litigation "Climate change litigation") is increasingly used as a tool to strengthen [climate action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_action "Climate action") from public institutions and companies. Activists also initiate lawsuits which target governments and demand that they take ambitious action or enforce existing laws on climate change.[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-435) Lawsuits against fossil-fuel companies generally seek compensation for [loss and damage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loss_and_damage_(climate_change) "Loss and damage (climate change)").[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-436) On 23 July 2025, the UN's [International Court of Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice "International Court of Justice") issued its advisory opinion, saying explicitly that states must act to stop climate change, and if they fail to accomplish that duty, other states can sue them. This obligation includes implementing their commitments in international agreements they are parties to, such as the 2015 Paris Climate Accord.[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-437)[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-438)[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-439)

History
-------

### Early discoveries

[![Image 46](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/18560823_Eunice_Newton_Foote_-_greenhouse_effect.png/500px-18560823_Eunice_Newton_Foote_-_greenhouse_effect.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:18560823_Eunice_Newton_Foote_-_greenhouse_effect.png)

[Eunice Newton Foote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eunice_Newton_Foote "Eunice Newton Foote") showed carbon dioxide's [heat-capturing effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greenhouse_effect "Greenhouse effect") in 1856, forseeing its implications for the planet.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Foote1856-440) (Carbon dioxide was called "carbonic acid gas".)

Scientists in the 19th century such as [Alexander von Humboldt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt "Alexander von Humboldt") began to foresee the effects of climate change.[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Nord_2020_p._51-441)[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Mukherjee_Scanlon_Aureli_Langan_2020_p._331-442)[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-von_Humboldt_Wulf_2018_p._10-443)[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Erdkamp_Manning_Verboven_2021_p._6-444) In the 1820s, [Joseph Fourier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Fourier "Joseph Fourier") proposed the greenhouse effect to explain why Earth's temperature was higher than the Sun's energy alone could explain. Earth's atmosphere is transparent to sunlight, so sunlight reaches the surface where it is converted to heat. However, the atmosphere is not transparent to heat radiating from the surface, and captures some of that heat, which in turn warms the planet.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-445) In 1856 [Eunice Newton Foote](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eunice_Newton_Foote "Eunice Newton Foote") demonstrated that the warming effect of the Sun is greater for air with water vapour than for dry air, and that the effect is even greater with carbon dioxide (CO 2). In "Circumstances Affecting the Heat of the Sun's Rays" she concluded that "[a]n atmosphere of that gas would give to our earth a high temperature".[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-:2-446)[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-447)

[![Image 47](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/19120814_Coal_Consumption_Affecting_Climate_-_Rodney_and_Otamatea_Times.jpg/500px-19120814_Coal_Consumption_Affecting_Climate_-_Rodney_and_Otamatea_Times.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:19120814_Coal_Consumption_Affecting_Climate_-_Rodney_and_Otamatea_Times.jpg)

This 1912 article succinctly describes the greenhouse effect, how burning coal creates carbon dioxide to cause global warming and climate change.[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Otamatea_Times-448)

Starting in 1859,[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-449)[John Tyndall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Tyndall "John Tyndall") established that nitrogen and oxygen—together totalling 99% of dry air—are transparent to radiated heat. However, water vapour and gases such as methane and carbon dioxide absorb radiated heat and re-radiate that heat into the atmosphere. Tyndall proposed that changes in the concentrations of these gases may have caused climatic changes in the past, including [ice ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_age "Ice age").[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-450)

[Svante Arrhenius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Svante_Arrhenius "Svante Arrhenius") noted that water vapour in air continuously varied, but the CO 2 concentration in air was influenced by long-term geological processes. Warming from increased CO 2 levels would increase the amount of water vapour, amplifying warming in a positive feedback loop. In 1896, he published the first [climate model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_model "Climate model") of its kind, projecting that halving CO 2 levels could have produced a drop in temperature initiating an ice age. Arrhenius calculated the temperature increase expected from doubling CO 2 to be around 5–6°C.[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-FOOTNOTELapenis1998-451) Other scientists were initially sceptical and believed that the greenhouse effect was saturated so that adding more CO 2 would make no difference, and that the climate would be self-regulating.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Weart_The_Carbon_Dioxide_Greenhouse_Effect-452) Beginning in 1938, [Guy Stewart Callendar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_Stewart_Callendar "Guy Stewart Callendar") published evidence that climate was warming and CO 2 levels were rising,[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-453) but his calculations met the same objections.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Weart_The_Carbon_Dioxide_Greenhouse_Effect-452)

### Development of a scientific consensus

[![Image 48](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/20211103_Academic_studies_of_scientific_consensus_-_global_warming%2C_climate_change_-_vertical_bar_chart_-_en.svg/500px-20211103_Academic_studies_of_scientific_consensus_-_global_warming%2C_climate_change_-_vertical_bar_chart_-_en.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:20211103_Academic_studies_of_scientific_consensus_-_global_warming,_climate_change_-_vertical_bar_chart_-_en.svg)

_Scientific consensus on causation:_ Academic studies of scientific agreement on human-caused global warming among climate experts (2010–2015) reflect that the level of consensus correlates with expertise in climate science.[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-454) A 2019 study found scientific consensus to be at 100%,[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Powell2019-455) and a 2021 study concluded that consensus exceeded 99%.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Lynas2021-456) Another 2021 study found that 98.7% of climate experts indicated that the Earth is getting warmer mostly because of human activity.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Myers2021-457)

In the 1950s, [Gilbert Plass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilbert_Plass "Gilbert Plass") created a detailed computer model that included different atmospheric layers and the infrared spectrum. This model predicted that increasing CO 2 levels would cause warming. Around the same time, [Hans Suess](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Suess "Hans Suess") found evidence that CO 2 levels had been rising, and [Roger Revelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Revelle "Roger Revelle") showed that the oceans would not absorb the increase. The two scientists subsequently helped [Charles Keeling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_David_Keeling "Charles David Keeling") to begin a record of continued increase—the "[Keeling Curve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keeling_Curve "Keeling Curve")"[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Weart_The_Carbon_Dioxide_Greenhouse_Effect-452)—which was part of continued scientific investigation through the 1960s into possible human causation of global warming.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-458) Studies such as the [National Research Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Academies_of_Sciences,_Engineering,_and_Medicine "National Academies of Sciences, Engineering, and Medicine")'s 1979 [Charney Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charney_Report "Charney Report") supported the accuracy of climate models that forecast significant warming.[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Charney1979-459) Human causation of observed global warming and dangers of unmitigated warming were publicly presented in [James Hansen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Hansen "James Hansen")'s 1988 testimony before a [US Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") committee.[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-nyt19880624-460)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-history.aip.org2-39) The [Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change "Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change") (IPCC), set up in 1988 to provide formal advice to the world's governments, spurred [interdisciplinary research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interdisciplinarity "Interdisciplinarity").[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-461) As part of the [IPCC reports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change#Assessment_reports "Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change"), scientists assess the scientific discussion that takes place in [peer-reviewed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer_review "Peer review")[journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_journal "Scientific journal") articles.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-462)

There is a nearly unanimous scientific consensus that the climate is warming and that this is caused by human activities.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Lynas2021-456) No scientific body of national or international standing [disagrees with this view](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_consensus_on_climate_change#Opposing "Scientific consensus on climate change").[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-463) As of 2019, agreement in recent literature reached over 99%.[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Powell2019-455)[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Lynas2021-456) The 2021 IPCC Assessment Report stated that it is "unequivocal" that climate change is caused by humans.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-Lynas2021-456) Consensus has further developed that action should be taken to protect people against the impacts of climate change. National science academies have called on world leaders to cut global emissions.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-464)

### Recent developments

[Extreme event attribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_event_attribution "Extreme event attribution") (EEA), also known as attribution science, was developed in the early decades of the 21st century.[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-AMS_20161201-465) EEA uses [climate models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_model "Climate model") to identify and quantify the role that human-caused climate change plays in the frequency, intensity, duration, and impacts of specific individual [extreme weather events](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_weather "Extreme weather").[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-466)[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-ClimateCentral_20241118-467) Results of attribution studies allow scientists and journalists to make statements such as, "this weather event was made at least _n_ times more likely by human-caused climate change" or "this heatwave was made _m_ degrees hotter than it would have been in a world without global warming" or "this event was effectively impossible without climate change".[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-WWA_2021-468) Greater computing power in the 2000s and conceptual breakthroughs in the early to mid 2010s[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-ScientificAmerican_20170102-469) enabled attribution science to detect the effects of climate change on some events with high confidence.[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-AMS_20161201-465) Scientists use methods that have already been [peer reviewed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer_review "Peer review"), allowing "rapid attribution studies" to be published within a "[news cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/24-hour_news_cycle "24-hour news cycle")" time frame.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_note-ScientificAmerican_20170102-469)

Climate change... contributed to desertification and land degradation in many regions (high confidence)."
    *   [IPCC AR6 WG2 SPM 2022](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFIPCC_AR6_WG2_SPM2022), p.9: "Observed increases in areas burned by wildfires have been attributed to human-induced climate change in some regions (medium to high confidence)"

CDR would be used to compensate for residual emissions and, in most cases, achieve net negative emissions to return global warming to 1.5°C following a peak (high confidence). CDR deployment of several hundreds of GtCO 2 is subject to multiple feasibility and sustainability constraints (high confidence)."

35.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_ref-35)**[Shaftel 2016](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFShaftel2016): "'Climate change' and 'global warming' are often used interchangeably but have distinct meanings.... Global warming refers to the upward temperature trend across the entire Earth since the early 20th century... Climate change refers to a broad range of global phenomena...[which] include the increased temperature trends described by global warming."
36.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_ref-36)**[Associated Press, 22 September 2015](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFAssociated_Press,_22_September2015): "The terms global warming and climate change can be used interchangeably. Climate change is more accurate scientifically to describe the various effects of greenhouse gases on the world because it includes extreme weather, storms and changes in rainfall patterns, ocean acidification and sea level.".
37.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_ref-37)**[IPCC AR5 SYR Glossary 2014](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFIPCC_AR5_SYR_Glossary2014), p.120: "Climate change refers to a change in the state of the climate that can be identified (e.g., by using statistical tests) by changes in the mean and/or the variability of its properties and that persists for an extended period, typically decades or longer. Climate change may be due to natural internal processes or external forcings such as modulations of the solar cycles, volcanic eruptions and persistent anthropogenic changes in the composition of the atmosphere or in land use."

This conclusion is not drawn from any one source of data but is based on multiple lines of evidence, including three worldwide temperature datasets showing nearly identical warming trends as well as numerous other independent indicators of global warming (e.g. rising sea levels, shrinking Arctic sea ice)."

154.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_ref-154)**[IPCC AR4 WG1 Ch9 2007](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFIPCC_AR4_WG1_Ch92007), pp.702–703; [Randel et al. 2009](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#CITEREFRandelShineAustinBarnett2009).
155.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change#cite_ref-155)**Greicius, Tony (2 August 2022). ["Tonga eruption blasted unprecedented amount of water into stratosphere"](https://climate.nasa.gov/news/3204/tonga-eruption-blasted-unprecedented-amount-of-water-into-stratosphere/). _NASA Global Climate Change_. Retrieved 18 January 2024. Massive volcanic eruptions like Krakatoa and Mount Pinatubo typically cool Earth's surface by ejecting gases, dust, and ash that reflect sunlight back into space. In contrast, the Tonga volcano didn't inject large amounts of aerosols into the stratosphere, and the huge amounts of water vapor from the eruption may have a small, temporary warming effect, since water vapor traps heat. The effect would dissipate when the extra water vapor cycles out of the stratosphere and would not be enough to noticeably exacerbate climate change effects.
